<div id="review_1301719771" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1301719771">
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546201072p2/3030788.jpg"></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1301719771?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1301719771" class="readable">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6517198890317935122">1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1301719771" rel="nofollow">The Name of the Wind</a> ★★★★★<br>2.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1451675878?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow">The Wise Man's Fear</a> ★★★★★<br>2.4) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904011753" rel="nofollow">The Lightning Tree</a> ★★★★★<br>2.5) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1458441355" rel="nofollow">The Slow Regard of Silent Things</a> ★★★★★<br>3.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1458404578" rel="nofollow">Doors of Stone</a> n/a<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451168104i/17513247._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I always feel like when I write a review for a five star book I'm not doing the book justice. It's easy for me to write what worked or what didn't work, but it's hard for me to describe magic. The book even touches on this and how it's impossible to describe some things. It would be easier</span>
  <span id="freeText6517198890317935122" style="display:none">1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1301719771" rel="nofollow">The Name of the Wind</a> ★★★★★<br>2.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1451675878?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow">The Wise Man's Fear</a> ★★★★★<br>2.4) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904011753" rel="nofollow">The Lightning Tree</a> ★★★★★<br>2.5) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1458441355" rel="nofollow">The Slow Regard of Silent Things</a> ★★★★★<br>3.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1458404578" rel="nofollow">Doors of Stone</a> n/a<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451168104i/17513247._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I always feel like when I write a review for a five star book I'm not doing the book justice. It's easy for me to write what worked or what didn't work, but it's hard for me to describe magic. The book even touches on this and how it's impossible to describe some things. It would be easier for me just to call this book <s>blue</s> fantastic and move on.<br><br>But where is the fun in that? So I'll try and probably do a mediocre attempt of explaining why the biggest regret I've made in my literary life is not reading this book sooner.<br><br><i>“Words are pale shadows of forgotten names. As names have power, words have power. Words can light fires in the minds of men. Words can wring tears from the hardest hearts.”</i><br><br><i> The Name of the Wind</i> has been on my "to-read" list forever, but what made me push it to the top was that I've been watching Pat <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/patrickrothfuss" rel="nofollow">stream</a> <a href="http://store.steampowered.com/app/377160/" rel="nofollow">Fallout 4</a> for a charity he runs, <a href="https://www.classy.org/events/worldbuilders-fundraiser-2015/e61518" rel="nofollow">Worldbuilders</a> (which I cannot stress enough how wonderful this cause is and how you should check it out). I always have some stream running in the background when I'm home and I figured I'd give him a chance, but I didn't expect to completely fall in love with his personality. Seriously, the man has more charisma than any of the Twitch streamers out there. He's very entertaining, passionate (about this charity, books, and his post-apocalyptic city), and a natural born storyteller (much like Kvothe). I liked Mr. Rothfuss so much that I knew I had to read his book immediately and, to know surprise, it completely enthralled me. In fact, it's the best fantasy book I've ever read. <br><br>The story starts in The Waystone Inn, in Neware. The owner, Kvothe/Kote, is going to tell his life's story to a scribe named Chronicler after the town has had a couple run-ins with "demons". I know the sound of an innkeeper telling a story of his past in his inn sounds a little cliché, but the story itself is so unique and good you will soon forget this is a tale being told from an inn at all.<br><br>Kvothe is a very gifted child and picks up everything he does with ease. His family's troupe (traveling performance artists) is one of the best in the world. Therefore, Kvothe has dipped in many different pools to excel at. His family accepts an arcanist named Abenthy (Ben) into their troupe and Kvothe soon finds a new best friend in him. He teaches Kvothe many different abilities, most including tricks with his mind. He also teaches him more about the world and a place called The University, which could help shape Kvothe's very gifted mind. unfortunately, Ben leaves the troupe to settle down and Kvothe, his wonderful parents, and all the other performers move on with their travels. <br><br>Disaster strikes and poor Kvothe soon learns the meaning of really being alone. His talented father is obsessed with writing a song about The Chandrian, who are a group of seven known in myth and folklore as bad or evil. Many people in this world fear different things, but everyone throughout Termerant fears The Chandrian. Soon, Kvothe understands why. <br><br><i>“My parents danced together, her head on his chest. Both had their eyes closed. They seemed so perfectly content. If you can find someone like that, someone who you can hold and close your eyes to the world with, then you're lucky. Even if it only lasts for a minute or a day.”</i><br><br>The rest is Kvothe's journey and what has made him become the man he is today, in The Waystone Inn, telling his story. I really don't want to say much more, I just hope I've swayed you into giving this series a shot if you were like me and haven't done so yet. <br><br>The story is fantastic, the writing is amazing, and if you have a heart the main character will capture it. Oh, and the goose bumps I got when reading the epilogue and blissfully being connected to the very beginning for a full circle. I don't really have words, just a whole lot of feelings that I'm not sure what to do with. I cannot wait to start <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1451675878" rel="nofollow">The Wise Man's Fear</a> after reading this first masterpiece.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448472474i/17146348._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“Go out in the early days of winter, after the first cold snap of the season. Find a pool of water with a sheet of ice across the top, still fresh and new and clear as glass. Near the shore the ice will hold you. Slide out farther. Farther. Eventually you'll find the place where the surface just barely bears your weight. There you will feel what I felt. The ice splinters under your feet. Look down and you can see the white cracks darting through the ice like mad, elaborate spiderwebs. It is perfectly silent, but you can feel the sudden sharp vibrations through the bottoms of your feet. That is what happened when Denna smiled at me.”</i><br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6517198890317935122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2303536005" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2303536005">
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg"></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2303536005?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2303536005" class="readable">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3923909068433549897">One of the best high fantasy books I’ve read.<br><br>No doubt there is a great deal of ink that comes along with Patrick Rothfuss’s debut novel of his Kingkiller series, many and well deserved high accolades, but I was surprised at just how good it was.<br><br>And there were no battle axe wielding ogres anywhere!<br><br>While much has been written about the influence Tolkien has had over the fantasy genre and also a lot of discussion about works that distinguish from his template, Rothfuss seems to have borrowed what is best from the good profess</span>
  <span id="freeText3923909068433549897" style="display:none">One of the best high fantasy books I’ve read.<br><br>No doubt there is a great deal of ink that comes along with Patrick Rothfuss’s debut novel of his Kingkiller series, many and well deserved high accolades, but I was surprised at just how good it was.<br><br>And there were no battle axe wielding ogres anywhere!<br><br>While much has been written about the influence Tolkien has had over the fantasy genre and also a lot of discussion about works that distinguish from his template, Rothfuss seems to have borrowed what is best from the good professor and then taken off to make this story his own. <br><br>And while this is high fantasy – meaning that it is a made-up world, medieval in appearance but with magic – this has more of the feel of an urban fantasy as the magic is below the surface and at least misunderstood. And if I had to make a comparison with a Tolkien book, I’d say this was more Hobbit than Lord of the Rings. This is more musical and personal than Tolkien’s great epic and also, because of the narrative approach of a traveler recalling past events, this has a “there and back again” quality.<br><br>Because of the bildungsroman elements of Kvothe’s story, this may draw some comparisons to JK Rowling’s work, but this is more complicated and of more spiritual depth than a Harry Potter story, and this is not YA.<br><br>The picaresque qualities of the book, and something about the style as well, made me think more of Jack Vance’s writing and some of the wonderful characters he created both in his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/951749.The_Dying_Earth__The_Dying_Earth___1_" title="The Dying Earth (The Dying Earth, #1) by Jack Vance" rel="nofollow">The Dying Earth</a> stories as well as his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6386834.The_Complete_Lyonesse__Lyonesse__1_3_" title="The Complete Lyonesse (Lyonesse #1-3) by Jack Vance" rel="nofollow">The Complete Lyonesse</a> books. <br><br>Kvothe is a red headed rogue who knows how to play the system – fundamentally good (I’d say Neutral or Chaotic Good in the old D&amp;D alignment system) but also mischievous enough to stay in trouble (and tell a good tale).<br><br>This is of course, as hundreds of thousands of fantasy readers know, about the life and times of Kvothe the Maedre, Dulator, Shadicar, Lightfinger, Six-String, Kvothe the Bloodless, Kvothe the Arcane, Kvothe Kingkiller. <br><br>Let’s face it – Kvothe the book seller, as this is wildly popular and deservedly so.<br><br>A scribe finds our hero laying low out on the fringe of society and convinces him to tell his story and the narrative that ensues is both entertaining and riveting. Rothfuss is a gifted writer and this is only just south of a masterpiece (though I’m sure many would disagree with me and go ahead and assign it that tribute). In this story, Rothfuss has made a list of all the elements necessary for a great fantasy work and then loaded in some more just to make it all the better.<br><br>I’ll be reading more from him, highly recommended.<br><br>** 2019 and I am reading the sequel and it's also very good.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548275567i/26961541.jpg" width="400" height="266" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3923909068433549897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

HIGHEST POSSIBLE RECOMMENDATION!! Read it!!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vvW/jINGdejNxuOZoHuQ6dF57d8g1RRX2UOxQtF+jtU2MwC3i+2YB4RvmtNk9Q7cMMxbpUE7UiW1/sHuhTWJ2A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xMRlwtPuIig7qw+Xoy5vk80MOhEpMQv2mwanUTEmjZFMAtr520XPx3ICdt1noPGmLLmMa0jfTYT3u9f9ZW2KnA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/108424.Patrick_Rothfuss">About Patrick Rothfuss</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="bookAuthorProfile">
<div class="bookAuthorProfile__topContainer">
<div class="bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer">
<a href="/author/show/108424.Patrick_Rothfuss"><div class="bookAuthorProfile__photo" style="background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1351307341p3/108424.jpg);"></div>

<div class="bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer">
<div class="bookAuthorProfile__name">
<a href="/author/show/108424.Patrick_Rothfuss">Patrick Rothfuss

<div class="bookAuthorProfile__about">

<span id="freeTextContainer3767161560291742429">It all began when Pat Rothfuss was born to a marvelous set of parents. Throughout his formative years they encouraged him to do his best, gave him good advice, and were no doubt appropriately dismayed when he failed to live up to his full potential.<br><br>In high-school Pat was something of a class clown. His hobbies included reading a novel or two a day and giving relationship advice to all</span>
  <span id="freeText3767161560291742429" style="display:none">It all began when Pat Rothfuss was born to a marvelous set of parents. Throughout his formative years they encouraged him to do his best, gave him good advice, and were no doubt appropriately dismayed when he failed to live up to his full potential.<br><br>In high-school Pat was something of a class clown. His hobbies included reading a novel or two a day and giving relationship advice to all his friends despite the fact that he had never so much as kissed a girl. He also role-played and wrote terrible stories about elves. He was pretty much a geek.<br><br>Most of Pat's adult life has been spent in the University Wisconsin Stevens Point. In 1991 he started college in order to pursue a career in chemical engineering, then he considered clinical psychology. In 1993 he quit pretending he knew what he wanted to do with his life, changed his major to "undecided," and proceeded to study whatever amused him. He also began writing a book....<br><br>For the next seven years Pat studied anthropology, philosophy, eastern religions, history, alchemy, parapsychology, literature, and writing. He studied six different martial arts, practiced improv comedy, learned how to pick locks, and became a skilled lover of women. He also began writing a satirical advice column which he continues to this day: The College Survivial Guide. Through all of this he continued to work on his novel.<br><br>In 2000 Pat went to grad school for English literature. Grad school sucked and Pat hated it. However, Pat learned that he loved to teach. He left in 2002 with his masters degree, shaking the dust from his feet and vowing never to return. During this period of time his novel was rejected by roughly every agent in the known universe.<br><br>Now Pat teaches half-time at his old school as an assistant-sub-lecturer. He is underpaid but generally left alone to do as he sees fit with his classes. He is advisor for the college feminists, the fencing club, and, oddly enough, a sorority. He still roll-plays occasionally, but now he does it in an extremely sophisticated, debonair way.<br><br>Through a series of lucky breaks, he has wound up with the best agent and editor imaginable, and the first book of his trilogy has been published under the title "The Name of the Wind." <br><br>Though it has only been out since April 2007, it has already been sold in 26 foreign countries and won several awards. <br><br>Pat has been described as "a rough, earthy iconoclast with a pipeline to the divine in everyone's subconscious." But honestly, that person was pretty drunk at the time, so you might want to take it with a grain of salt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3767161560291742429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
